## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Kubernetes Server-Side Apply Configuration Guide

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a deep guide for applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply semantics, including conflict handling and workflow patterns.

## Scope

Focus on the applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

502026-03-11T07:23:49.733806agentmessage-
I am thinking...: I now have a comprehensive understanding of the Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations subsystem. Let me organize my findings before writing the documentation:

## Key Components

### 1. Client-Side: `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations`
- Generated types (e.g., `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`) with all-pointer fields
- `With<FieldName>` builder methods for fluent construction
- `Extract<Kind>` functions for the extract/modify/apply workflow
- `internal/internal.go` - embedded YAML schema for SMD type parsing
- `utils.go` - `NewTypeConverter` factory and `ForKind()` dispatch function

### 2. Client Transport: `k8s.io/client-go/util/apply` and `k8s.io/client-go/gentype`
- `apply.NewRequest()` - marshals the apply config to JSON/CBOR and sets Content-Type to `application/apply-patch+yaml` (or `+cbor`)
- `gentype.alsoApplier.Apply()` - calls `apply.NewRequest()` and sends the PATCH request
- `gentype.ClientWithListAndApply` - the generic client type used by all typed clients

### 3. Server-Side Entry Point: `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`
- `PatchResource()` - HTTP handler that dispatches based on Content-Type
- For `ApplyYAMLPatchType` / `ApplyCBORPatchType`: creates `applyPatcher` via `newApplyPatcher()`
- `patcher.patchResource()` - sets up the mechanism and calls `GuaranteedUpdate` via `finisher.FinishRequest`
- `fieldmanager.NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` wraps admission to protect managedFields

- **Field manager core** — public API (`fieldmanager.go`, `extract.go`, `scalehandler.go`) and the internal decorator chain

*managedfields.FieldManager\\n444: }\\n445: \\n446: func (p *smpPatcher) applyPatchToCurrentObject(requestContext context.Context, currentObject runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\\n447: \\t// Let me organize my findings before writing the documentation:\n\n## Key Components\n\n### 1. Client-Side: `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations`\n- Generated types (e.g., `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`) with all-pointer fields\n- `With<FieldName>` builder methods for fluent construction\n- `Extract<Kind>` functions for the extract/modify/apply workflow\n- `internal/internal.go` - embedded YAML schema for SMD type parsing\n- `utils.go` - `NewTypeConverter` factory and `ForKind()` dispatch function\n\n### 2. Client Transport: `k8s.io/client-go/util/apply` and `k8s.io/client-go/gentype`\n- `apply.NewRequest()` - marshals the apply config to JSON/CBOR and sets Content-Type to `application/apply-patch+yaml` (or `+cbor`)\n- `gentype.alsoApplier.Apply()` - calls `apply.NewRequest()` and sends the PATCH request\n- `gentype.ClientWithListAndApply` - the generic client type used by all typed clients\n\n### 3. Server-Side Entry Point: `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`\n- `PatchResource()` - HTTP handler that dispatches based on Content-Type\n- For `ApplyYAMLPatchType` / `ApplyCBORPatchType`: creates `applyPatcher` via `newApplyPatcher()`\n- `patcher.patchResource()` - sets up the mechanism and calls `GuaranteedUpdate` via `finisher.FinishRequest`\n- `fieldmanager.NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` wraps admission to protect managedFields\n\n### 4. Field Manager Core: `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields`\n- `fieldmanager.go` - public API: `NewDefaultFieldManager`, `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager`, `ValidateManagedFields`\n- `typeconverter.go` - `TypeConverter` interface, `NewTypeConverter` (OpenAPI-based), `NewDeducedTypeConverter` (CRD fallback), `NewSchemeTypeConverter` (scheme-based)\n- `extract.go` - `ExtractInto()` for the extract/modify/apply workflow\n- `scalehandler.go` - `ScaleHandler` for translating managed fields between main resource and scale subresource\n\n### 5. Internal Manager Chain: `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal`\nThe `NewDefaultFieldManager` builds a decorator chain (outermost to innermost):\n1. `versionCheckManager` - validates GVK of applied object\n2. `lastAppliedUpdater` - syncs `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation for kubectl\n3. `lastAppliedManager` - handles CSA\u2192SSA migration for kubectl\n4. `skipNonAppliedManager` (probabilistic) - skips tracking for objects that haven't been applied yet\n5. `capManagersManager` - caps update managers at `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers=10`, merging oldest into \"ancient-changes\" bucket\n6. `buildManagerInfoManager` - builds the JSON manager identifier (name+operation+version+subresource)\n7. `managedFieldsUpdater` - timestamps updates, merges same-manager fields\n8. `stripMetaManager` - removes system fields (apiVersion, kind, metadata.name, etc.) from managed field sets\n9. `structuredMergeManager` (innermost) - calls `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6/merge.Updater`\n\n### 6. Structured Merge Diff: `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6`\n- `merge.Updater` - the actual merge engine\n- `fieldpath.ManagedFields` - map of manager identifier \u2192 `VersionedSet`\n- `typed.TypedValue` - schema-aware typed representation\n- `merge.Conflicts` - list of `{Manager, Path}` conflict pairs\n\n### 7. Managed Fields Encoding: `internal/managedfields.go`\n- `DecodeManagedFields` / `EncodeObjectManagedFields` - wire format \u2194 internal format\n- `BuildManagerIdentifier` - JSON-serialized manager key (excludes time, fields, fieldsType; excludes APIVersion for appliers)\n- `ManagedInterface` - `Fields() fieldpath.ManagedFields` + `Times() map[string]*metav1.Time`\n\n### 8. Admission Integration: `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`\n- `NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` - wraps admission, validates managedFields after mutation, resets if invalid\n\n### 9. Code Generation: `k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen`\n- Generates the `*ApplyConfiguration` types from Go API types\n- `ExternalApplyConfigurations` map for cross-package references\n\n## End-to-End Flow\n\n### Apply Request Flow:\n1. Client builds `DeploymentApplyConfiguration` using `With*` methods\n2. `alsoApplier.Apply()` calls `apply.NewRequest()` \u2192 marshals to JSON, sets Content-Type `application/apply-patch+yaml`\n3. HTTP PATCH request reaches `PatchResource()` handler\n4. `patcher.patchResource()` creates `applyPatcher` mechanism\n5. `finisher.FinishRequest()` calls `restPatcher.Update()` with `GuaranteedUpdate`\n6. `GuaranteedUpdate` calls `p.applyPatch()` \u2192 `mechanism.applyPatchToCurrentObject()`\n7. `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject()` calls `scope.FieldManager.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, manager, force)`\n8. `FieldManager.Apply()` decodes live object's managedFields, calls manager chain\n9. Manager chain: versionCheck \u2192 lastAppliedUpdater \u2192 lastAppliedManager \u2192 skipNonApplied \u2192 capManagers \u2192 buildManagerInfo \u2192 managedFieldsUpdater \u2192 stripMeta \u2192 structuredMergeManager\n10. `structuredMergeManager.Apply()` converts objects to typed values, calls `merge.Updater.Apply()`\n11. SMD library performs structured merge, returns new typed object + updated managed fields\n12. If conflicts: returns `merge.Conflicts` \u2192 `NewConflictError()` \u2192 HTTP 409\n13. If force=true: conflicts are overridden, fields taken from other managers\n14. Result encoded back to object, managedFields re-encoded, returned to client\n\n### Extract/Modify/Apply Workflow:\n1. `ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldMgr)` calls `managedfields.ExtractInto()`\n2. `ExtractInto()` finds the manager's `ManagedFieldsEntry` (operation=Apply)\n3. Decodes `FieldsV1` JSON into `fieldpath.Set`\n4. Calls `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` to get only owned fields\n5. Converts to unstructured, then to `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`\n6. User modifies the extracted config\n7. Calls `Apply()` with the modified config\n\n## Conflict Handling\n- Conflict = a field in the apply config is already owned by a different manager\n- `merge.Conflicts` is a list of `{Manager string, Path fieldpath.Path}`\n- `NewConflictError()` converts to `StatusError` with `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict` causes\n- Error message: \"Apply failed with N conflicts: conflicts with \"manager\": - .path.to.field\"\n- Resolution: `Force: true` in `ApplyOptions` \u2192 `force=true` in `FieldManager.Apply()` \u2192 SMD takes ownership\n\n## CSA\u2192SSA Migration\n- `lastAppliedManager`: when manager=\"kubectl\" and conflicts exist, checks if conflicts are covered by `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation\n- If all conflicts are in last-applied fields that match live object, force-applies (migration path)\n- `lastAppliedUpdater`: after successful apply with manager=\"kubectl\", updates the last-applied annotation\n\n## CRD vs Built-in Resources\n- Built-in: `NewStructuredMergeManager` with `typeConverter` (OpenAPI-based), `versionConverter` (hub-based)\n- CRD: `NewCRDStructuredMergeManager` with `deducedTypeConverter` (all fields atomic), `crdVersionConverter` (direct hub)\n- CRD without schema: all fields treated as atomic (no granular merge)\n\n## Manager Identifier\n- For Apply: `{\"manager\":\"kubectl\",\"operation\":\"Apply\",\"subresource\":\"\"}` (no APIVersion, no time, no fields)\n- For Update: `{\"manager\":\"kubectl\",\"operation\":\"Update\",\"apiVersion\":\"apps/v1\",\"subresource\":\"\"}` (includes APIVersion)\n- This means an applier always has the same identifier regardless of which version they applied\n\n## Performance/Operational Notes\n- `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10`: caps the number of update manager entries, merging oldest into \"ancient-changes\" bucket\n- `DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1`: 100% probability of tracking on create (can be tuned)\n- `UpdateNoErrors`: silently clears managedFields on error (logged at most once per second via `AtMostEvery`)\n- `isTooLargeError`: if object too large, retries with managedFields stripped (only for non-apply patches)\n- `stripMetaManager`: removes system fields from managed field sets to avoid tracking them\n- Schema embedded in `internal/internal.go` as YAML string, parsed once via `sync.Once`\n\nNow I have enough to write a comprehensive documentation.\n"
}

[Key Components and Responsibility Split](#2-key-components-and-responsibility-split)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [Conflict Handling](#4-conflict-handling)\n5. [File and Directory Map](#11-file-and-directory-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### What Server-Side Apply Solves\n\nBefore Server-Side Apply (SSA), Kubernetes clients used either full `PUT` updates or `kubectl apply`'s client-side three-way merge. Both approaches had a fundamental problem: when multiple actors (a human operator, a controller, an autoscaler) each managed different fields of the same object, they would overwrite each other's changes. The client-side apply annotation (`kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration`) was a partial workaround, but it was fragile, annotation-size-limited, and not available to non-kubectl clients.\n\nSSA moves the merge logic to the API server. Each actor declares only the fields it cares about (its \"apply configuration\"), and the server tracks which actor owns which fields. When two actors try to own the same field, the server returns a conflict error rather than silently overwriting.\n\n### The applyconfigurations Package\n\nThe `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations` package provides the client-side representation of an apply configuration. The core insight is that standard Go API structs (e.g., `appsv1.Deployment`) cannot represent \"I want to set `spec.replicas` to 0 and say nothing about `spec.template`\" because Go zero values are indistinguishable from absent fields. The apply configuration types solve this by making every field a pointer:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment.go\ntype DeploymentApplyConfiguration struct {\n    metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration    `json:\",inline\"`\n    *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec   *DeploymentSpecApplyConfiguration   `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status *DeploymentStatusApplyConfiguration `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n```\n\nA nil pointer field is omitted from JSON serialization entirely, so only the fields the caller explicitly sets appear in the apply request body.\n\n### Upstream and Downstream Dependencies\n\n**Upstream (what SSA depends on):**\n- `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6` \u2014 the external library that implements the actual field-level merge algorithm, conflict detection, and field ownership tracking. This is the most critical external dependency.\n- `k8s.io/kube-openapi` \u2014 provides the OpenAPI schema that the type converter uses to understand field types, list merge keys, and atomicity.\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime` \u2014 object conversion, serialization, and the `ObjectConvertor` interface used to translate between API versions.\n\n**Downstream (what depends on SSA):**\n- Every typed client in `k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/...` exposes `Apply()` and `ApplyStatus()` methods.\n- The `kubectl apply --server-side` command.\n- Controllers that use the extract/modify/apply pattern.\n- The fake client (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/fake/clientset_generated.go`) uses `applyconfigurations.NewTypeConverter(scheme)` to support SSA in tests.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe subsystem is organized into four distinct layers, each with a clear responsibility boundary.\n\n### Layer 1: Generated Apply Configuration Types (`k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Provide a type-safe, pointer-based Go representation of every Kubernetes API object suitable for constructing apply requests.\n\nEvery resource kind has a corresponding `*ApplyConfiguration` struct. These are generated by `applyconfiguration-gen` (in `staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/`) from the Go API types. The generator reads the `ExternalApplyConfigurations` map to handle cross-package type references:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/args/args.go\nExternalApplyConfigurations map[types.Name]string\n// Example: k8s.io/api/apps/v1.Deployment:k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/apps/v1\n```\n\nEach generated type provides:\n- `With<FieldName>` builder methods that return the receiver for chaining.\n- `Extract<Kind>` and `Extract<Kind>From` functions for the extract/modify/apply workflow.\n- An `IsApplyConfiguration()` marker method.\n\nThe `internal/internal.go` file (also generated) embeds the complete SMD schema as a YAML string and exposes a `Parser()` function that parses it once via `sync.Once`. This schema is used by `ExtractInto` to understand field types when extracting owned fields.\n\nThe top-level `utils.go` provides `ForKind(schema.GroupVersionKind) applyconfiguration` \u2014 a dispatch function that returns an empty apply configuration for any known GVK, used by the fake client's type converter.\n\n### Layer 2: Client Transport (`k8s.io/client-go/util/apply`, `k8s.io/client-go/gentype`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Marshal the apply configuration and send it as an HTTP PATCH request with the correct Content-Type.\n\n`apply.NewRequest()` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/apply/apply.go`) is the single function that bridges the apply configuration to the REST client:\n\n```go\nfunc NewRequest(client rest.Interface, applyConfiguration interface{}) (*rest.Request, error) {\n    pt := types.ApplyYAMLPatchType\n    marshal := json.Marshal\n    if features.FeatureGates().Enabled(features.ClientsAllowCBOR) &&\n       features.FeatureGates().Enabled(features.ClientsPreferCBOR) {\n        pt = types.ApplyCBORPatchType\n        marshal = cbor.Marshal\n    }\n    body, err := marshal(applyConfiguration)\n    // ...\n    return client.Patch(pt).Body(body), nil\n}\n```\n\nThe `gentype` package (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/gentype/type.go`) provides the generic `alsoApplier[T, C]` mixin that all typed clients embed:\n\n```go\nfunc (a *alsoApplier[T, C]) Apply(ctx context.Context, obj C, opts metav1.ApplyOptions) (T, error) {\n    patchOpts := opts.ToPatchOptions()\n    request, err := apply.NewRequest(a.client.client, obj)\n    // ...\n    err = request.\n        NamespaceIfScoped(a.client.namespace, ...).\n        Resource(a.client.resource).\n        Name(*obj.GetName()).\n        VersionedParams(&patchOpts, a.client.parameterCodec).\n        Do(ctx).Into(result)\n    return result, err\n}\n```\n\n`metav1.ApplyOptions.ToPatchOptions()` converts `FieldManager`, `Force`, and `DryRun` into `PatchOptions` query parameters that the server reads.\n\n### Layer 3: Server-Side Handler (`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Receive the PATCH request, dispatch to the correct patch mechanism, run admission, and persist the result.\n\n`PatchResource()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` is the HTTP handler for all PATCH operations. It dispatches based on Content-Type:\n\n```go\n// patch.go lines 672-687\ncase types.ApplyYAMLPatchType:\n    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, yaml.Unmarshal, yaml.UnmarshalStrict)\n    p.forceAllowCreate = true\ncase types.ApplyCBORPatchType:\n    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, cbor.Unmarshal, cbor.Unmarshal)\n    p.forceAllowCreate = true\n```\n\nSetting `forceAllowCreate = true` means an apply request will create the object if it does not exist (upsert semantics).\n\nThe admission chain is wrapped by `fieldmanager.NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`), which snapshots `managedFields` before admission and restores them if a mutating webhook corrupts the field:\n\n```go\nmanagedFieldsBeforeAdmission := objectMeta.GetManagedFields()\nif err := mutationInterface.Admit(ctx, a, o); err != nil { return err }\nif err := managedfields.ValidateManagedFields(managedFieldsAfterAdmission); err != nil {\n    objectMeta.SetManagedFields(managedFieldsBeforeAdmission)\n    warning.AddWarning(ctx, \"\", fmt.Sprintf(InvalidManagedFieldsAfterMutatingAdmissionWarningFormat, err.Error()))\n}\n```\n\nThe `patcher.patchResource()` method assembles a transformer chain `[applyPatch, applyAdmission, dedupOwnerReferences]` and passes it to `rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo`, which `GuaranteedUpdate` calls on each retry.\n\n### Layer 4: Field Manager Core (`k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Implement the field ownership tracking and structured merge logic.\n\nThis layer is split into a public API surface and an internal implementation.\n\n**Public API** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/`):\n- `fieldmanager.go`: `NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` \u2014 factory functions that assemble the manager decorator chain.\n- `typeconverter.go`: `TypeConverter` interface and three implementations: `NewTypeConverter` (OpenAPI-based), `NewDeducedTypeConverter` (CRD fallback), `NewSchemeTypeConverter` (scheme-based, added in 2025).\n- `extract.go`: `ExtractInto()` \u2014 the server-side logic for the extract/modify/apply workflow.\n- `scalehandler.go`: `ScaleHandler` \u2014 translates managed fields between a main resource and its `scale` subresource.\n\n**Internal implementation** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/`):\n- `manager.go`: The `Manager` interface with `Update()` and `Apply()` methods.\n- `fieldmanager.go`: `FieldManager` struct \u2014 the public entry point that decodes/encodes managed fields and calls the manager chain.\n- `structuredmerge.go`: `structuredMergeManager` \u2014 the innermost manager that calls the SMD library.\n- `managedfields.go`: Wire format encoding/decoding (`DecodeManagedFields`, `EncodeObjectManagedFields`, `BuildManagerIdentifier`).\n- Decorator managers: `versionCheckManager`, `lastAppliedUpdater`, `lastAppliedManager`, `skipNonAppliedManager`, `capManagersManager`, `buildManagerInfoManager`, `managedFieldsUpdater`, `stripMetaManager`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Client Side\n\nA controller builds an apply configuration and calls `Apply()`:\n\n```go\n// Based on staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go\nhpaApplyConfig := v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(autoscalerName, ns).\n    WithSpec(v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().WithMinReplicas(0))\nresult, err := hpav1client.Apply(ctx, hpaApplyConfig,\n    metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"mycontroller\", Force: true})\n```\n\n`alsoApplier.Apply()` calls `apply.NewRequest()`, which marshals the config to JSON (or CBOR if feature gates are set) and creates a `rest.Request` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`. The request is sent as `PATCH /apis/autoscaling/v1/namespaces/{ns}/horizontalpodautoscalers/{name}?fieldManager=mycontroller&force=true`.\n\n### 3.2 Server Entry Point\n\n`PatchResource()` reads the body, parses `PatchOptions` from query parameters, and wraps the admission chain with `NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController`. It creates a `patcher` struct and calls `p.patchResource()`.\n\n`patchResource()` creates an `applyPatcher` mechanism and assembles the transformer chain. It calls `finisher.FinishRequest()`, which runs the request in a goroutine with a timeout. Inside, it calls `p.restPatcher.Update()` with `p.updatedObjectInfo` (the transformer chain).\n\n### 3.3 GuaranteedUpdate Loop\n\nThe storage layer's `GuaranteedUpdate` reads the current live object from etcd, then calls the transformer chain:\n\n1. **`p.applyPatch`**: If the live object has no UID (does not exist), calls `mechanism.createNewObject()`. Otherwise calls `mechanism.applyPatchToCurrentObject()`.\n\n2. **`applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject()`**: Deserializes the request body into an unstructured object, then calls `scope.FieldManager.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, manager, force)`.\n\n3. **`p.applyAdmission`**: Runs the admission chain (mutating webhooks, etc.) on the result.\n\n4. **`dedupOwnerReferencesTransformer`**: Deduplicates owner references.\n\n### 3.4 FieldManager.Apply() \u2014 The Manager Chain\n\n`FieldManager.Apply()` in `internal/fieldmanager.go` decodes the live object's `managedFields` from the wire format, then calls the manager chain:\n\n```go\n// internal/fieldmanager.go\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (object runtime.Object, err error) {\n    managed, err := DecodeManagedFields(accessor.GetManagedFields())\n    object, managed, err = f.fieldManager.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managed, manager, force)\n    if err != nil {\n        if conflicts, ok := err.(merge.Conflicts); ok {\n            return nil, NewConflictError(conflicts)\n        }\n        return nil, err\n    }\n    if err = EncodeObjectManagedFields(object, managed); err != nil { ... }\n    return object, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe manager chain is assembled in `NewDefaultFieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go`):\n\n```go\nNewVersionCheckManager(\n    NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n        NewLastAppliedManager(\n            NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n                NewCapManagersManager(\n                    NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n                        NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n                            NewStripMetaManager(f), // f = structuredMergeManager\n                        ), kind.GroupVersion(), subresource,\n                    ), DefaultMaxUpdateManagers,\n                ), objectCreater, DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability,\n            ), typeConverter, objectConverter, kind.GroupVersion(),\n        ),\n    ), kind,\n), subresource,\n```\n\nEach decorator wraps the next, calling through on the happy path and adding its own logic:\n\n| Decorator | Apply behavior |\n|-----------|---------------|\n| `versionCheckManager` | Rejects if `appliedObj.GVK != expected GVK` |\n| `lastAppliedUpdater` | After success, if manager=\"kubectl\" and last-applied annotation exists, updates it |\n| `lastAppliedManager` | If manager=\"kubectl\" and conflicts exist, checks if they're covered by last-applied annotation; if so, force-applies (CSA\u2192SSA migration) |\n| `skipNonAppliedManager` | If managed fields are empty, bootstraps them from the live object before applying |\n| `capManagersManager` | Pass-through for Apply (only caps update managers) |\n| `buildManagerInfoManager` | Converts manager name to JSON identifier: `{\"manager\":\"ctrl\",\"operation\":\"Apply\",\"subresource\":\"\"}` |\n| `managedFieldsUpdater` | After success, sets `managed.Times()[fieldManager] = now` |\n| `stripMetaManager` | After success, removes system fields (apiVersion, kind, metadata.name, etc.) from the manager's field set |\n| `structuredMergeManager` | Calls `merge.Updater.Apply()` |\n\n### 3.5 structuredMergeManager.Apply()\n\nThis is where the actual merge happens (`internal/structuredmerge.go`):\n\n```go\nfunc (f *structuredMergeManager) Apply(liveObj, patchObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error) {\n    // Validate: patch must not contain managedFields\n    if patchObjMeta.GetManagedFields() != nil {\n        return nil, nil, errors.NewBadRequest(\"metadata.managedFields must be nil\")\n    }\n    // Convert to SMD typed values\n    patchObjTyped, _ := f.typeConverter.ObjectToTyped(patchObj)\n    liveObjTyped, _ := f.typeConverter.ObjectToTyped(liveObjVersioned, typed.AllowDuplicates)\n    // Call SMD merge\n    newObjTyped, managedFields, err := f.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)\n    // Convert back\n    newObj, _ := f.typeConverter.TypedToObject(newObjTyped)\n    newObjVersioned, _ := f.toVersioned(newObj)\n    f.objectDefaulter.Default(newObjVersioned)\n    newObjUnversioned, _ := f.toUnversioned(newObjVersioned)\n    return newObjUnversioned, managed, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe `TypeConverter` converts between `runtime.Object` and `typed.TypedValue`. For built-in types, it uses the OpenAPI schema indexed by GVK. For CRDs, it uses `deducedTypeConverter` which treats all fields as atomic.\n\nThe `versionConverter` (passed to `merge.Updater.Converter`) handles cross-version field tracking: when the SMD library needs to compare fields across versions, it calls `Convert()`, which goes through the Kubernetes hub version (internal type) as an intermediate.\n\n### 3.6 Response\n\nIf `merge.Updater.Apply()` returns conflicts and `force=false`, `FieldManager.Apply()` calls `NewConflictError()` which produces an HTTP 409 with `StatusCause` entries. If `force=true`, the SMD library takes ownership of the conflicting fields and returns the merged object. The result is encoded back to the object, `managedFields` is re-encoded onto it, and it is persisted to etcd.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Conflict Handling\n\n### What Constitutes a Conflict\n\nA conflict occurs when a field in the apply configuration is already owned by a different field manager. \"Owned\" means the field appears in another manager's `FieldsV1` set with `operation=Apply`. Fields owned by `operation=Update` managers do not cause conflicts \u2014 they are simply overwritten.\n\n### Conflict Error Structure\n\n`NewConflictError()` in `internal/conflict.go` converts `merge.Conflicts` (a list of `{Manager string, Path fieldpath.Path}`) into a `StatusError`:\n\n```go\nfunc NewConflictError(conflicts merge.Conflicts) *errors.StatusError {\n    causes := []metav1.StatusCause{}\n    for _, conflict := range conflicts {\n        causes = append(causes, metav1.StatusCause{\n            Type:    metav1.CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict,\n            Message: fmt.Sprintf(\"conflict with %v\", printManager(conflict.Manager)),\n            Field:   conflict.Path.String(),\n        })\n    }\n    return errors.NewApplyConflict(causes, getConflictMessage(conflicts))\n}\n```\n\nThe `printManager()` function deserializes the JSON manager identifier to produce a human-readable string like `\"kubectl\" using apps/v1 at 2024-01-15T10:00:00Z`.\n\nA single-conflict error looks like:\n```\nApply failed with 1 conflict: conflict with \"other-controller\": .spec.replicas\n```\n\nMultiple conflicts are grouped by manager:\n```\nApply failed with 3 conflicts:\nconflicts with \"other-controller\":\n- .spec.replicas\n- .spec.template.spec.containers[name=\"app\"].image\n```\n\n### Resolving Conflicts\n\n**Option 1: Force apply.** Set `Force: true` in `ApplyOptions`. The SMD library will take ownership of the conflicting fields, removing them from the previous owner's field set. This is appropriate for controllers that are authoritative for their fields.\n\n**Option 2: Remove the field from the apply configuration.** If the controller does not need to own the field, simply omit it from the apply configuration. The field will remain in the live object, owned by whoever set it.\n\n**Option 3: Use the extract/modify/apply pattern.** Extract only the fields the controller already owns, modify them, and re-apply. This avoids accidentally claiming new fields.\n\n### Force Apply Semantics\n\nWhen `force=true`, the SMD library's `Apply()` method takes ownership of all fields in the apply configuration, regardless of who previously owned them. The previous owner's field set is updated to remove those fields. If the previous owner's field set becomes empty, their `ManagedFieldsEntry` is removed entirely.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Client-Side Apply Workflow Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Full Reconciliation (Recommended for New Controllers)\n\nThe controller reconstructs the complete apply configuration on every reconciliation loop:\n\n```go\n// Based on staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go\nhpaApplyConfig := v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(autoscalerName, ns).\n    WithSpec(v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().WithMinReplicas(0))\nreturn hpav1client.Apply(ctx, hpaApplyConfig,\n    metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"mycontroller\", Force: true})\n```\n\nThis is the simplest pattern. The controller always sets `Force: true` because it is authoritative for its fields. If a field is removed from the apply configuration, it is released from the controller's ownership (and may be garbage-collected if no other manager owns it).\n\n### Pattern 2: Extract/Modify/Apply (For Incremental Updates)\n\nWhen a controller only needs to update a subset of fields it already owns, it can extract its current state and modify it in place:\n\n```go\n// Based on staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go\nfieldMgr := \"my-field-manager\"\ndeployment, err := deploymentClient.Get(ctx, \"example-deployment\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n// Extract only the fields owned by this manager\ndeploymentApplyConfig, err := appsv1ac.ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldMgr)\n// Modify in place\ndeploymentApplyConfig.Spec.Template.Spec.WithContainers(\n    corev1ac.Container().WithName(\"app\").WithImage(\"nginx:1.14.2\"),\n)\n// Apply\napplied, err := deploymentClient.Apply(ctx, deploymentApplyConfig,\n    metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: fieldMgr})\n```\n\n`ExtractDeployment()` calls `ExtractDeploymentFrom()` which calls `managedfields.ExtractInto()`:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment.go\nfunc ExtractDeploymentFrom(deployment *appsv1.Deployment, fieldManager string, subresource string) (*DeploymentApplyConfiguration, error) {\n    b := &DeploymentApplyConfiguration{}\n    err := managedfields.ExtractInto(deployment, internal.Parser().Type(\"io.k8s.api.apps.v1.Deployment\"), fieldManager, b, subresource)\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n`ExtractInto()` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go`) finds the manager's `ManagedFieldsEntry` (filtering for `operation=Apply`), decodes the `FieldsV1` JSON into a `fieldpath.Set`, calls `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` to get only the leaf values owned by this manager, and converts the result back to the apply configuration type.\n\n**Important limitation:** `ExtractInto` only works with root resource objects. Subresource objects (e.g., `autoscaling.Scale` from the `scale` subresource) do not carry their own `managedFields`. The `scale` subresource is handled specially by `ScaleHandler` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/scalehandler.go`), which translates field paths between the main resource and the scale subresource.\n\n### Pattern 3: Subresource Apply\n\nApply configurations can target subresources. The `ApplyStatus()` method applies to the `status` subresource:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/gentype/type.go\nfunc (a *alsoApplier[T, C]) ApplyStatus(ctx context.Context, obj C, opts metav1.ApplyOptions) (T, error) {\n    // ...\n    err = request.\n        Resource(a.client.resource).\n        Name(*obj.GetName()).\n        SubResource(\"status\").\n        // ...\n}\n```\n\nThe `FieldManager.Apply()` call on the server side uses the `subresource` field in the manager identifier, so status managers are tracked separately from spec managers.\n\n---\n\n## 6. CSA-to-SSA Migration\n\nObjects managed by `kubectl apply` (client-side apply) carry the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation. When such an object is first touched by `kubectl apply --server-side`, the `lastAppliedManager` decorator handles the migration transparently.\n\n### Migration Logic (`internal/lastappliedmanager.go`)\n\nWhen `manager=\"kubectl\"` and the initial SSA apply produces conflicts:\n\n1. The decorator calls `allowedConflictsFromLastApplied(liveObj)` to compute the set of fields that were in the last-applied annotation and still match the live object.\n2. If all conflicts are within this allowed set, the decorator calls `f.fieldManager.Apply(..., force=true)` \u2014 effectively force-applying only the fields that kubectl previously owned.\n3. If any conflict is outside the allowed set (i.e., another actor changed a field that kubectl used to own), the conflict is surfaced to the user.\n\nThis means a migration from CSA to SSA is conflict-free as long as no other actor has modified the fields kubectl was managing.\n\n### Annotation Sync (`internal/lastappliedupdater.go`)\n\nAfter a successful SSA apply with `manager=\"kubectl\"`, the `lastAppliedUpdater` decorator updates the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation to reflect the new applied configuration. This keeps the annotation in sync for any tooling that still reads it.\n\nThe annotation is only updated if it already exists on the object \u2014 the updater does not create it from scratch. This prevents SSA from accidentally adding the annotation to objects that were never managed by CSA.\n\n---\n\n## 7. CRD vs Built-in Resource Handling\n\n### Built-in Resources\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` uses `NewStructuredMergeManager` with:\n- `typeConverter`: OpenAPI-based, built from the server's OpenAPI spec. Maps each GVK to a `typed.ParseableType` using the `x-kubernetes-group-version-kind` extension.\n- `versionConverter`: Hub-based. When SMD needs to compare fields across versions, it converts through the internal (hub) version: `versioned \u2192 hub \u2192 target versioned`.\n\nThe OpenAPI schema encodes list merge semantics (e.g., `x-kubernetes-list-map-keys: [name]` for containers) so that SMD can merge lists by key rather than treating them as atomic.\n\n### CRD Resources\n\n`NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` uses `NewCRDStructuredMergeManager` with:\n- `typeConverter`: `deducedTypeConverter` if no schema is available, or an OpenAPI-based converter if the CRD has a structural schema.\n- `versionConverter`: CRD-based. Uses the hub version directly (no group-based hub lookup).\n\n```go\n// internal/typeconverter.go\n// DeducedTypeConverter is a TypeConverter for CRDs that don't have a schema.\n// CRDs are merged with all their fields being \"atomic\" (lists included).\nfunc NewDeducedTypeConverter() TypeConverter {\n    return deducedTypeConverter{}\n}\n```\n\nWhen a CRD has no schema, all fields are treated as atomic: lists are replaced wholesale rather than merged by key. This is safe but loses granularity \u2014 two controllers cannot independently manage different elements of the same list.\n\nWhen a CRD has a structural schema with `x-kubernetes-list-map-keys`, the OpenAPI-based converter is used and list merging works the same as for built-in types.\n\n### The `NewSchemeTypeConverter` (Added 2025)\n\n`internal/runtimetypeconverter.go` introduces `schemeTypeConverter`, which uses `scheme.ToOpenAPIDefinitionName(gvk)` to look up the type name and then uses a pre-built `typed.Parser`. This allows the type converter to be constructed from a `runtime.Scheme` and a parser, without requiring the full OpenAPI spec map. It is used in contexts where the scheme is available but the OpenAPI spec is not.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Failure Mode: managedFields Corruption by Admission Webhooks\n\nMutating admission webhooks can modify `metadata.managedFields`. If a webhook sets managedFields to an invalid value (wrong format, missing required fields), subsequent apply operations will fail with decode errors.\n\nThe `managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`) mitigates this by:\n1. Snapshotting managedFields before admission.\n2. Validating managedFields after admission using `managedfields.ValidateManagedFields()`.\n3. If invalid, restoring the pre-admission snapshot and emitting a warning to the client.\n\nThe warning format is: `.metadata.managedFields was in an invalid state after admission; this could be caused by an outdated mutating admission controller; please fix your requests: <error>`.\n\n### Failure Mode: Object Too Large\n\nIf an object exceeds the etcd size limit after a patch, the server retries with managedFields stripped:\n\n```go\n// patch.go\nif isTooLargeError(err) && p.patchType != types.ApplyYAMLPatchType && p.patchType != types.ApplyCBORPatchType {\n    p.updatedObjectInfo = rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo(nil,\n        p.applyPatch, p.applyAdmission, dedupOwnerReferencesTransformer,\n        func(_ context.Context, obj, _ runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\n            accessor.SetManagedFields(nil)\n            return obj, nil\n        })\n    result, err = requestFunc()\n}\n```\n\nNote that this fallback is explicitly disabled for apply requests (`ApplyYAMLPatchType`, `ApplyCBORPatchType`). For apply, managedFields are essential to the operation and cannot be stripped. If an apply request produces an object that is too large, it will fail with a 422 error.\n\n### Failure Mode: UpdateNoErrors Silent Degradation\n\n`FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors()` (`internal/fieldmanager.go`) is used for non-apply operations (create, update, patch). If managedFields tracking fails for any reason, it silently clears managedFields and logs the error at most once per second:\n\n```go\nfunc (f *FieldManager) UpdateNoErrors(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, manager string) runtime.Object {\n    obj, err := f.Update(liveObj, newObj, manager)\n    if err != nil {\n        atMostEverySecond.Do(func() {\n            klog.ErrorS(err, \"[SHOULD NOT HAPPEN] failed to update managedFields\", ...)\n        })\n        RemoveObjectManagedFields(newObj)\n        return newObj\n    }\n    return obj\n}\n```\n\nThis means a bug in the managedFields tracking code will not break normal CRUD operations, but will silently degrade SSA functionality. The `[SHOULD NOT HAPPEN]` log message is the signal to look for.\n\n### Limit: DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10\n\nThe `capManagersManager` (`internal/capmanagers.go`) caps the number of update-operation manager entries at 10. When exceeded, the oldest entries are merged into versioned \"ancient-changes\" buckets:\n\n```go\nconst DefaultMaxUpdateManagers int = 10\n// ...\noldUpdatesManagerName: \"ancient-changes\",\n```\n\nThe merge is by API version: all old update entries for the same version are unioned into a single `ancient-changes` entry. This prevents unbounded growth of `managedFields` in objects that are updated by many different actors over time.\n\n**Tradeoff:** Once entries are merged into \"ancient-changes\", the individual manager attribution is lost. If a field was owned by \"controller-A\" and gets merged into \"ancient-changes\", a subsequent apply by another controller will not see a conflict for that field (since \"ancient-changes\" is not an apply manager). This can lead to unexpected field ownership changes.\n\n### Limit: DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1\n\n`skipNonAppliedManager` (`internal/skipnonapplied.go`) uses a probability to decide whether to start tracking managedFields on object creation:\n\n```go\nconst DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability float32 = 1\n```\n\nAt probability 1.0, all creates are tracked. This was introduced to allow gradual rollout of SSA tracking on existing clusters where many objects were created before SSA was enabled. At probability < 1.0, some creates would not be tracked, and tracking would only begin on the first apply.\n\n### Design Tradeoff: Manager Identifier Excludes APIVersion for Appliers\n\n`BuildManagerIdentifier()` (`internal/managedfields.go`) deliberately excludes `APIVersion` from the manager identifier for apply operations:\n\n```go\nif encodedManager.Operation == metav1.ManagedFieldsOperationApply {\n    encodedManagerCopy.APIVersion = \"\"\n}\n```\n\nThis means a controller that applies `apps/v1` today and `apps/v2` tomorrow is treated as the same manager. Without this, every API version upgrade would create a new manager entry and leave orphaned entries from the old version. The tradeoff is that the manager identifier does not encode which version was last applied.\n\nFor update operations, APIVersion is included in the identifier, so different versions of an updater are tracked separately.\n\n### Design Tradeoff: stripMetaManager Excludes System Fields\n\n`stripMetaManager` (`internal/stripmeta.go`) removes a hardcoded set of fields from every manager's field set after each operation:\n\n```go\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"apiVersion\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"kind\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"name\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"namespace\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"creationTimestamp\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"selfLink\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"uid\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"clusterName\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"generation\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"managedFields\"),\nfieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"metadata\", \"resourceVersion\"),\n```\n\nThese fields are either server-managed (UID, resourceVersion, generation) or universal (apiVersion, kind, name, namespace). Tracking them would create spurious conflicts between every actor that sets them. The tradeoff is that these fields can never be \"owned\" by any manager, so no conflict will ever be raised for them.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 9.1 Custom TypeConverter\n\nThe `TypeConverter` interface (`internal/typeconverter.go`) is the primary extension point for integrating custom type systems:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nThree implementations are provided:\n- `NewTypeConverter(openapiSpec, preserveUnknownFields)` \u2014 for resources with OpenAPI schemas.\n- `NewDeducedTypeConverter()` \u2014 for resources without schemas (atomic merge).\n- `NewSchemeTypeConverter(scheme, parser)` \u2014 for scheme-based type lookup.\n\nA custom implementation could, for example, use a different schema format or provide special merge semantics for a custom resource type. The risk is that an incorrect implementation will produce wrong field ownership tracking, leading to spurious conflicts or missed conflicts.\n\n### 9.2 resetFields Filter\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` accept a `resetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter` parameter. This is passed to `merge.Updater.IgnoreFilter` in the SMD library. Fields matching the filter are excluded from ownership tracking \u2014 they are always reset to their server-side values and never cause conflicts.\n\nThis is used for fields that the server always sets (e.g., `status` fields that are managed by the server, not the client). The risk of misconfiguring this is that fields that should cause conflicts will be silently ignored.\n\n### 9.3 Subresource Field Path Mappings (ScaleHandler)\n\n`ScaleHandler` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/scalehandler.go`) is used by resources that expose a `scale` subresource. It translates field paths between the main resource and the scale subresource using a `ResourcePathMappings` map:\n\n```go\ntype ResourcePathMappings map[string]fieldpath.Path\n// Example: \"apps/v1\" -> fieldpath.MakePathOrDie(\"spec\", \"replicas\")\n```\n\nCustom resources that implement a scale subresource must provide their own path mappings. An incorrect mapping will cause the `spec.replicas` field to be attributed to the wrong manager.\n\n### 9.4 applyconfiguration-gen for Custom Types\n\nThe `applyconfiguration-gen` tool can generate apply configuration types for custom API types. The `ExternalApplyConfigurations` argument maps external types to their apply configuration packages:\n\n```\nk8s.io/api/apps/v1.Deployment:k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/apps/v1\n```\n\nThis allows generated types for custom resources to reference built-in apply configuration types (e.g., `PodTemplateSpecApplyConfiguration`) without re-generating them.\n\n### 9.5 Fake Client Integration\n\nThe fake client (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/fake/clientset_generated.go`) uses `applyconfigurations.NewTypeConverter(scheme)` to support SSA in tests:\n\n```go\napplyconfigurations.NewTypeConverter(scheme)\n```\n\nThis creates a `TypeConverter` from the scheme's registered types, allowing the fake client to perform real field ownership tracking in unit tests. Custom fake clients for custom resources should do the same.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n**Schema parsing cost:** The SMD schema embedded in `internal/internal.go` is parsed once at startup via `sync.Once`. The schema is large (covering all built-in Kubernetes types) and parsing it takes non-trivial time. This is amortized across all requests, but it means the first apply request after process startup will be slower.\n\n**Per-request cost:** Each apply request requires:\n1. Decoding the live object's `managedFields` from JSON.\n2. Converting both the live object and the patch object to SMD `TypedValue` (involves schema validation).\n3. Running the SMD merge algorithm (O(fields) complexity).\n4. Re-encoding `managedFields` to JSON.\n\nFor objects with many fields and many managers, this can be significant. The `bench_test.go` files in the fieldmanager package provide benchmarks.\n\n**managedFields size:** `managedFields` is stored inline in the object in etcd. For objects with many managers (e.g., a Deployment touched by many controllers), `managedFields` can grow large. The `capManagersManager` limits update managers to 10, but apply managers are not capped. An object with 50 different apply managers will have 50 `ManagedFieldsEntry` records.\n\n**Retry overhead:** `GuaranteedUpdate` retries on conflict. Each retry re-reads from etcd and re-runs the transformer chain, including the full SMD merge. High-contention objects (many concurrent applies) will experience retry amplification.\n\n### Reliability\n\n**Admission webhook compatibility:** Mutating webhooks that modify `managedFields` directly are a reliability risk. The `managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` provides a safety net, but it only restores the pre-admission state \u2014 it does not prevent the webhook from running or warn the webhook author. Webhooks should avoid touching `managedFields`.\n\n**Version skew:** The manager identifier for apply operations excludes APIVersion. If a controller is upgraded and starts applying a different API version, it will be treated as the same manager. This is generally correct, but if the field paths change between versions (e.g., a field is renamed), the old field set in `managedFields` may reference paths that no longer exist in the new version. The SMD library handles this gracefully (missing paths are ignored), but it can leave stale entries.\n\n**CRD schema changes:** If a CRD's schema changes (e.g., a list gains `x-kubernetes-list-map-keys`), existing `managedFields` entries were computed under the old schema. The SMD library will re-interpret them under the new schema on the next apply, which may produce unexpected results. There is no migration mechanism for this.\n\n### Maintainability\n\n**Generated code:** The `*ApplyConfiguration` types and `internal/internal.go` are generated. They must be regenerated whenever the API types change. The `hack/update-codegen.sh` script handles this. Forgetting to regenerate will cause the apply configuration types to be out of sync with the API types, leading to missing fields or incorrect field paths.\n\n**Manager identifier stability:** The JSON manager identifier is used as a map key in `managedFields`. If the identifier format changes (e.g., new fields are added to `ManagedFieldsEntry`), existing entries in etcd will not be recognized as belonging to the same manager. This would cause every existing manager to appear as a new manager on the next operation, potentially creating duplicate entries. The `BuildManagerIdentifier` function is therefore very stable and changes to it require careful migration planning.\n\n**Debugging managedFields:** The `managedFields` field is visible in `kubectl get -o yaml` output. Each entry shows the manager name, operation, API version, timestamp, and the `FieldsV1` field set (in a compact binary-like format). The `kubectl alpha field-manager` subcommand (if available) can decode `FieldsV1` into human-readable field paths. Understanding the current ownership state is essential for diagnosing conflict errors.\n\n---\n\n## 11. File and Directory Map\n\nThe following files are the most important for understanding the SSA and applyconfigurations subsystem:\n\n### Client-Side Apply Configuration Types\n| Path | Purpose When two actors try to own the same field, the server returns a conflict error rather than silently overwriting.\n    26\t\n    27\t### The applyconfigurations Package\n    28\t\n    29\tThe `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations` package provides the client-side representation of an apply configuration. The core insight is that standard Go API structs (e.g., `appsv1.Deployment`) cannot represent \"I want to set `spec.replicas` to 0 and say nothing about `spec.template`\" because Go zero values are indistinguishable from absent fields. The apply configuration types solve this by making every field a pointer:\n    30\t\n    31\t```go\n    32\t// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment.go\n    33\ttype DeploymentApplyConfiguration struct {\n    34\t    metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration    `json:\",inline\"`\n    35\t    *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    36\t    Spec   *DeploymentSpecApplyConfiguration   `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    37\t    Status *DeploymentStatusApplyConfiguration `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n    38\t}\n    39\t```\n    40\t\n    41\tA nil pointer field is omitted from JSON serialization entirely, so only the fields the caller explicitly sets appear in the apply request body.\n    42\t\n    43\t### Upstream and Downstream Dependencies\n    44\t\n    45\t**Upstream (what SSA depends on):**\n    46\t- `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6` \u2014 the external library that implements the actual field-level merge algorithm, conflict detection, and field ownership tracking. This is the most critical external dependency.\n    47\t- `k8s.io/kube-openapi` \u2014 provides the OpenAPI schema that the type converter uses to understand field types, list merge keys, and atomicity.\n    48\t- `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime` \u2014 object conversion, serialization, and the `ObjectConvertor` interface used to translate between API versions.\n    49\t\n    50\t**Downstream (what depends on SSA):**\n    51\t- Every typed client in `k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/...` exposes `Apply()` and `ApplyStatus()` methods.\n    52\t- The `kubectl apply --server-side` command.\n    53\t- Controllers that use the extract/modify/apply pattern.\n    54\t- The fake client (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/fake/clientset_generated.go`) uses `applyconfigurations.NewTypeConverter(scheme)` to support SSA in tests.\n    55\t\n    56\t---\n    57\t\n    58\t## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n    59\t\n    60\tThe subsystem is organized into four distinct layers, each with a clear responsibility boundary.\n    61\t\n    62\t### Layer 1: Generated Apply Configuration Types (`k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations`)\n    63\t\n    64\t**Responsibility:** Provide a type-safe, pointer-based Go representation of every Kubernetes API object suitable for constructing apply requests.\n    65\t\n    66\tEvery resource kind has a corresponding `*ApplyConfiguration` struct. These are generated by `applyconfiguration-gen` (in `staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/`) from the Go API types. The generator reads the `ExternalApplyConfigurations` map to handle cross-package type references:\n    67\t\n    68\t```go\n    69\t// staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/args/args.go\n    70\tExternalApplyConfigurations map[types.Name]string\n    71\t// Example: k8s.io/api/apps/v1.Deployment:k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/apps/v1\n    72\t```\n    73\t\n    74\tEach generated type provides:\n    75\t- `With<FieldName>` builder methods that return the receiver for chaining.\n    76\t- `Extract<Kind>` and `Extract<Kind>From` functions for the extract/modify/apply workflow.\n    77\t- An `IsApplyConfiguration()` marker method.\n    78\t\n    79\tThe `internal/internal.go` file (also generated) embeds the complete SMD schema as a YAML string and exposes a `Parser()` function that parses it once via `sync.Once`. This schema is used by `ExtractInto` to understand field types when extracting owned fields.\n    80\t\n    81\tThe top-level `utils.go` provides `ForKind(schema.GroupVersionKind) applyconfiguration` \u2014 a dispatch function that returns an empty apply configuration for any known GVK, used by the fake client's type converter.\n    82\t\n    83\t### Layer 2: Client Transport (`k8s.io/client-go/util/apply`, `k8s.io/client-go/gentype`)\n    84\t\n    85\t**Responsibility:** Marshal the apply configuration and send it as an HTTP PATCH request with the correct Content-Type.\n    86\t\n    87\t`apply.NewRequest()` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/apply/apply.go`) is the single function that bridges the apply configuration to the REST client:\n    88\t\n    89\t```go\n    90\tfunc NewRequest(client rest.Interface, applyConfiguration interface{}) (*rest.Request, error) {\n    91\t    pt := types.ApplyYAMLPatchType\n    92\t    marshal := json.Marshal\n    93\t    if features.FeatureGates().Enabled(features.ClientsAllowCBOR) &&\n    94\t       features.FeatureGates().Enabled(features.ClientsPreferCBOR) {\n    95\t        pt = types.ApplyCBORPatchType\n    96\t        marshal = cbor.Marshal\n    97\t    }\n    98\t    body, err := marshal(applyConfiguration)\n    99\t    // ...\n   100\t    return client.Patch(pt).Body(body), nil\n   101\t}\n   102\t```\n   103\t\n   104\tThe `gentype` package (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/gentype/type.go`) provides the generic `alsoApplier[T, C]` mixin that all typed clients embed:\n   105\t\n   106\t```go\n   107\tfunc (a *alsoApplier[T, C]) Apply(ctx context.Context, obj C, opts metav1.ApplyOptions) (T, error) {\n   108\t    patchOpts := opts.ToPatchOptions()\n   109\t    request, err := apply.NewRequest(a.client.client, obj)\n   110\t    // ...\n   111\t    err = request.\n   112\t        NamespaceIfScoped(a.client.namespace, ...).\n   113\t        Resource(a.client.resource).\n   114\t        Name(*obj.GetName()).\n   115\t        VersionedParams(&patchOpts, a.client.parameterCodec).\n   116\t        Do(ctx).Into(result)\n   117\t    return result, err\n   118\t}\n   119\t```\n   120\t\n   121\t`metav1.ApplyOptions.ToPatchOptions()` converts `FieldManager`, `Force`, and `DryRun` into `PatchOptions` query parameters that the server reads.\n   122\t\n   123\t### Layer 3: Server-Side Handler (`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers`)\n   124\t\n   125\t**Responsibility:** Receive the PATCH request, dispatch to the correct patch mechanism, run admission, and persist the result.\n   126\t\n   127\t`PatchResource()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` is the HTTP handler for all PATCH operations. It dispatches based on Content-Type:\n   128\t\n   129\t```go\n   130\t// patch.go lines 672-687\n   131\tcase types.ApplyYAMLPatchType:\n   132\t    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, yaml.Unmarshal, yaml.UnmarshalStrict)\n   133\t    p.forceAllowCreate = true\n   134\tcase types.ApplyCBORPatchType:\n   135\t    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, cbor.Unmarshal, cbor.Unmarshal)\n   136\t    p.forceAllowCreate = true\n   137\t```\n   138\t\n   139\tSetting `forceAllowCreate = true` means an apply request will create the object if it does not exist (upsert semantics).\n   140\t\n   141\tThe admission chain is wrapped by `fieldmanager.NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`), which snapshots `managedFields` before admission and restores them if a mutating webhook corrupts the field:\n   142\t\n   143\t```go\n   144\tmanagedFieldsBeforeAdmission := objectMeta.GetManagedFields()\n   145\tif err := mutationInterface.Admit(ctx, a, o); err != nil { return err }\n   146\tif err := managedfields.ValidateManagedFields(managedFieldsAfterAdmission); err != nil {\n   147\t    objectMeta.SetManagedFields(managedFieldsBeforeAdmission)\n   148\t    warning.AddWarning(ctx, \"\", fmt.Sprintf(InvalidManagedFieldsAfterMutatingAdmissionWarningFormat, err.Error()))\n   149\t}\n   150\t```\n   151\t\n   152\tThe `patcher.patchResource()` method assembles a transformer chain `[applyPatch, applyAdmission, dedupOwnerReferences]` and passes it to `rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo`, which `GuaranteedUpdate` calls on each retry.\n   153\t\n   154\t### Layer 4: Field Manager Core (`k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields`)\n   155\t\n   156\t**Responsibility:** Implement the field ownership tracking and structured merge logic.\n   157\t\n   158\tThis layer is split into a public API surface and an internal implementation.\n   159\t\n   160\t**Public API** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/`):\n   161\t- `fieldmanager.go`: `NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` \u2014 factory functions that assemble the manager decorator chain.\n   162\t- `typeconverter.go`: `TypeConverter` interface and three implementations: `NewTypeConverter` (OpenAPI-based), `NewDeducedTypeConverter` (CRD fallback), `NewSchemeTypeConverter` (scheme-based, added in 2025).\n   163\t- `extract.go`: `ExtractInto()` \u2014 the server-side logic for the extract/modify/apply workflow.\n   164\t- `scalehandler.go`: `ScaleHandler` \u2014 translates managed fields between a main resource and its `scale` subresource.\n   165\t\n   166\t**Internal implementation** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/`):\n   167\t- `manager.go`: The `Manager` interface with `Update()` and `Apply()` methods.\n   168\t- `fieldmanager.go`: `FieldManager` struct \u2014 the public entry point that decodes/encodes managed fields and calls the manager chain.\n   169\t- `structuredmerge.go`: `structuredMergeManager` \u2014 the innermost manager that calls the SMD library.\n   170\t- `managedfields.go`: Wire format encoding/decoding (`DecodeManagedFields`, `EncodeObjectManagedFields`, `BuildManagerIdentifier`).\n   171\t- Decorator managers: `versionCheckManager`, `lastAppliedUpdater`, `lastAppliedManager`, `skipNonAppliedManager`, `capManagersManager`, `buildManagerInfoManager`, `managedFieldsUpdater`, `stripMetaManager`.\n   172\t\n   173\t---\n   174\t\n   175\t## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n   176\t\n   177\t### 3.1 Client Side\n   178\t\n   179\tA controller builds an apply configuration and calls `Apply()`:\n   180\t\n   181\t```go\n   182\t// Based on staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go\n   183\thpaApplyConfig := v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(autoscalerName, ns).\n   184\t    WithSpec(v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().WithMinReplicas(0))\n   185\tresult, err := hpav1client.Apply(ctx, hpaApplyConfig,\n   186\t    metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"mycontroller\", Force: true})\n   187\t```\n   188\t\n   189\t`alsoApplier.Apply()` calls `apply.NewRequest()`, which marshals the config to JSON (or CBOR if feature gates are set) and creates a `rest.Request` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`. The request is sent as `PATCH /apis/autoscaling/v1/namespaces/{ns}/horizontalpodautoscalers/{name}?fieldManager=mycontroller&force=true`.\n   190\t\n   191\t### 3.2 Server Entry Point\n   192\t\n   193\t`PatchResource()` reads the body, parses `PatchOptions` from query parameters, and wraps the admission chain with `NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController`. It creates a `patcher` struct and calls `p.patchResource()`.\n   194\t\n   195\t`patchResource()` creates an `applyPatcher` mechanism and assembles the transformer chain. It calls `finisher.FinishRequest()`, which runs the request in a goroutine with a timeout. Inside, it calls `p.restPatcher.Update()` with `p.updatedObjectInfo` (the transformer chain).\n   196\t\n   197\t### 3.3 GuaranteedUpdate Loop\n   198\t\n   199\tThe storage layer's `GuaranteedUpdate` reads the current live object from etcd, then calls the transformer chain:\n   200\t\n   201\t1. **`p.applyPatch`**: If the live object has no UID (does not exist), calls `mechanism.createNewObject()`. Otherwise calls `mechanism.applyPatchToCurrentObject()`.\n   202\t\n   203\t2. **`applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject()`**: Deserializes the request body into an unstructured object, then calls `scope.FieldManager.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, manager, force)`.\n   204\t\n   205\t3. **`p.applyAdmission`**: Runs the admission chain (mutating webhooks, etc.) on the result.\n   206\t\n   207\t4. **`dedupOwnerReferencesTransformer`**: Deduplicates owner references.\n   208\t\n   209\t### 3.4 FieldManager.Apply() \u2014 The Manager Chain\n   210\t\n   211\t`FieldManager.Apply()` in `internal/fieldmanager.go` decodes the live object's `managedFields` from the wire format, then calls the manager chain:\n   212\t\n   213\t```go\n   214\t// internal/fieldmanager.go\n   215\tfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (object runtime.Object, err error) {\n   216\t    managed, err := DecodeManagedFields(accessor.GetManagedFields())\n   217\t    object, managed, err = f.fieldManager.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managed, manager, force)\n   218\t    if err != nil {\n   219\t        if conflicts, ok := err.(merge.Conflicts); ok {\n   220\t            return nil, NewConflictError(conflicts)\n   221\t        }\n   222\t        return nil, err\n   223\t    }\n   224\t    if err = EncodeObjectManagedFields(object, managed); err != nil { ... }\n   225\t    return object, nil\n   226\t}\n   227\t```\n   228\t\n   229\tThe manager chain is assembled in `NewDefaultFieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go`):\n   230\t\n   231\t```go\n   232\tNewVersionCheckManager(\n   233\t    NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n   234\t        NewLastAppliedManager(\n   235\t            NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n   236\t                NewCapManagersManager(\n   237\t                    NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n   238\t                        NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n   239\t                            NewStripMetaManager(f), // f = structuredMergeManager\n   240\t                        ), kind.GroupVersion(), subresource,\n   241\t                    ), DefaultMaxUpdateManagers,\n   242\t                ), objectCreater, DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability,\n   243\t            ), typeConverter, objectConverter, kind.GroupVersion(),\n   244\t        ),\n   245\t    ), kind,\n   246\t), subresource,\n   247\t```\n   248\t\n   249\tEach decorator wraps the next, calling through on the happy path and adding its own logic:\n   250\t\n   251\t| Decorator | Apply behavior |\n   252\t|-----------|---------------|\n   253\t| `versionCheckManager` | Rejects if `appliedObj.GVK != expected GVK` |\n   254\t| `lastAppliedUpdater` | After success, if manager=\"kubectl\" and last-applied annotation exists, updates it |\n   255\t| `lastAppliedManager` | If manager=\"kubectl\" and conflicts exist, checks if they're covered by last-applied annotation;
